"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form, custom Triton kernels.

Hand-written chunk-parallel KDA for RTX 3090 (SM86). Independent Triton
reimplementation of the standard chunked delta-rule decomposition:

  stage 1 (intra, parallel over b,h,chunk):
      gc = cumsum(g) within chunk;
      Aqk[c,j] = scale*<q_c e^{gc_c-gc_j}, k_j>   (j<=c)
      Akk[c,i] = beta_c*<k_c e^{gc_c-gc_i}, k_i>  (i<c, strict lower)
      Ainv = (I + Akk)^{-1}    (forward substitution, fp32)
      w = Ainv @ (beta * k * e^{gc});  u = Ainv @ (beta * v)
      kg = k * e^{gc_last - gc}
  stage 2 (scan, parallel over b,h,v-block; sequential over chunks):
      h[i] = S;  v_new = u - w@S;  S = diag(e^{gc_last})S + kg^T @ v_new
  stage 3 (output, parallel over b,h,chunk,v-block):
      o = scale*(q e^{gc}) @ h + tril(Aqk) @ v_new
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl


# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
# stage 1: intra-chunk (cumsum, Aqk, Akk, inverse, w, u, kg)
# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
@triton.jit
def _intra_kernel(
    q, k, v, g, beta,
    qg_out, gclast, w, u, kg, Aqk,
    T, NT,
    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
    NSTEP: tl.constexpr,
    scale,
):
    i_t = tl.program_id(0)
    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
    i_b = i_bh // H
    i_h = i_bh % H

    qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
    v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
    b_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h)
    a_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * BT

    o_t = tl.arange(0, BT)

    # ---- cumsum g within chunk ----
    p_g = tl.make_block_ptr(g + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
    b_g = tl.load(p_g, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
    b_gc = tl.cumsum(b_g, axis=0)  # (BT, K)

    # last-row cumsum (chunk total decay) -> tiny per-chunk buffer for the scan
    b_gc_last = tl.sum(tl.where((o_t == (BT - 1))[:, None], b_gc, 0.0), 0)  # (K,)
    gclast_off = ((i_b * NT + i_t) * H + i_h) * K
    tl.store(gclast + gclast_off + tl.arange(0, K), b_gc_last)

    eg = tl.exp(b_gc)         # e^{gc}
    egn = tl.exp(-b_gc)       # e^{-gc}

    p_q = tl.make_block_ptr(q + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
    p_k = tl.make_block_ptr(k + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
    p_v = tl.make_block_ptr(v + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
    b_q = tl.load(p_q, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
    b_k = tl.load(p_k, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
    b_v = tl.load(p_v, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)

    p_beta = tl.make_block_ptr(beta + b_base, (T,), (H,), (i_t * BT,), (BT,), (0,))
    b_beta = tl.load(p_beta, boundary_check=(0,)).to(tl.float32)

    # decayed factors as bf16 operands for the BTxBT tensor-core dots
    b_qg = (b_q * eg).to(tl.bfloat16)
    b_kgp = (b_k * eg).to(tl.bfloat16)
    b_kgm = (b_k * egn).to(tl.bfloat16)

    # store q*e^{gc} (decayed query) for the output kernel -> it reads this
    # directly instead of re-loading q and gc and recomputing the exp.
    p_qg = tl.make_block_ptr(qg_out + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_qg, b_qg, boundary_check=(0, 1))

    # Aqk (BT,BT), lower incl diag, scaled
    b_Aqk = tl.dot(b_qg, tl.trans(b_kgm)) * scale
    m_le = o_t[:, None] >= o_t[None, :]
    b_Aqk = tl.where(m_le, b_Aqk, 0.0)
    p_Aqk = tl.make_block_ptr(Aqk + a_base, (T, BT), (H * BT, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_Aqk, b_Aqk.to(Aqk.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))

    # Akk strict lower (L), fp32
    b_Akk = tl.dot(b_kgp, tl.trans(b_kgm)) * b_beta[:, None]
    m_lt = o_t[:, None] > o_t[None, :]
    b_L = tl.where(m_lt, b_Akk, 0.0)

    # ---- inverse of (I + L) via Neumann doubling ----
    # N = -L is strictly lower (nilpotent, N^BT = 0), so
    # (I+L)^{-1} = sum_i N^i = prod_j (I + N^{2^j}).  log2(BT) doubling steps,
    # each two BTxBT tensor-core matmuls instead of BT serial scalar steps.
    b_eye = (o_t[:, None] == o_t[None, :]).to(tl.float32)
    b_N = -b_L
    b_Ai = b_eye + b_N            # S_1 = sum_{i<2} N^i  (fp32 accumulator)
    b_P = b_N.to(tl.bfloat16)
    for _ in tl.static_range(NSTEP):   # each step doubles the term count
        b_P = tl.dot(b_P, b_P).to(tl.bfloat16)
        b_Ai = b_Ai + tl.dot(b_P, b_Ai.to(tl.bfloat16))

    # ---- w, u ----
    b_rhs_w = (b_beta[:, None] * b_k * eg).to(w.dtype.element_ty)
    b_rhs_u = (b_beta[:, None] * b_v).to(u.dtype.element_ty)
    b_Ai_c = b_Ai.to(w.dtype.element_ty)
    b_w = tl.dot(b_Ai_c, b_rhs_w)
    b_u = tl.dot(b_Ai_c, b_rhs_u)
    p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(w + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
    p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(u + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_w, b_w.to(w.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
    tl.store(p_u, b_u.to(u.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))

    # ---- kg = k * e^{gc_last - gc} ----
    b_kg = b_k * tl.exp(b_gc_last[None, :] - b_gc)
    p_kg = tl.make_block_ptr(kg + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_kg, b_kg.to(kg.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))


# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
# stage 2: sequential state scan -> h (per chunk state), v_new
# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
@triton.jit
def _scan_kernel(
    w, u, kg, gclast, h, v_new,
    T, NT,
    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
    BV: tl.constexpr, BK: tl.constexpr,
):
    i_v = tl.program_id(0)
    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
    i_b = i_bh // H
    i_h = i_bh % H

    o_k = tl.arange(0, K)

    # state accumulator (K, BV) fp32, K split into BK-blocks handled as full K here
    b_h = tl.zeros([K, BV], dtype=tl.float32)

    for i_t in range(NT):
        qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
        v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
        h_base = ((i_b * NT + i_t) * H + i_h) * K * V

        # store current state to h[i_t]
        p_h = tl.make_block_ptr(h + h_base, (K, V), (V, 1), (0, i_v * BV), (K, BV), (1, 0))
        tl.store(p_h, b_h.to(h.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))

        # v_new = u - w @ S
        p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(w + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
        b_w = tl.load(p_w, boundary_check=(0, 1))
        b_wh = tl.dot(b_w, b_h.to(b_w.dtype))  # (BT, BV)
        p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(u + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, i_v * BV), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
        b_vn = tl.load(p_u, boundary_check=(0, 1)) - b_wh
        p_vn = tl.make_block_ptr(v_new + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, i_v * BV), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
        tl.store(p_vn, b_vn.to(v_new.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))

        # decay state by e^{gc_last} (read tiny per-chunk gc_last buffer)
        gclast_off = ((i_b * NT + i_t) * H + i_h) * K
        b_gc_last = tl.load(gclast + gclast_off + o_k).to(tl.float32)  # (K,)
        b_h = b_h * tl.exp(b_gc_last)[:, None]

        # S += kg^T @ v_new
        p_kg = tl.make_block_ptr(kg + qk_base, (K, T), (1, H * K), (0, i_t * BT), (K, BT), (0, 1))
        b_kg = tl.load(p_kg, boundary_check=(0, 1))  # (K, BT)
        b_h += tl.dot(b_kg, b_vn.to(b_kg.dtype))


# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
# stage 3: output o = scale*(q e^{gc}) @ h + tril(Aqk) @ v_new
# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
@triton.jit
def _o_kernel(
    qg, h, Aqk, v_new, o,
    T, NT,
    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
    BV: tl.constexpr, BK: tl.constexpr,
    scale,
):
    i_v = tl.program_id(0)
    i_t = tl.program_id(1)
    i_bh = tl.program_id(2)
    i_b = i_bh // H
    i_h = i_bh % H

    qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
    v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
    a_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * BT
    h_base = ((i_b * NT + i_t) * H + i_h) * K * V

    o_t = tl.arange(0, BT)

    b_o = tl.zeros([BT, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
    for i_k in range(tl.cdiv(K, BK)):
        p_qg = tl.make_block_ptr(qg + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, i_k * BK), (BT, BK), (1, 0))
        p_h = tl.make_block_ptr(h + h_base, (K, V), (V, 1), (i_k * BK, i_v * BV), (BK, BV), (1, 0))
        b_qg = tl.load(p_qg, boundary_check=(0, 1))
        b_h = tl.load(p_h, boundary_check=(0, 1))
        b_o += tl.dot(b_qg, b_h)
    b_o *= scale

    p_A = tl.make_block_ptr(Aqk + a_base, (T, BT), (H * BT, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
    b_A = tl.load(p_A, boundary_check=(0, 1))
    m_le = o_t[:, None] >= o_t[None, :]
    b_A = tl.where(m_le, b_A, 0.0).to(v_new.dtype.element_ty)
    p_vn = tl.make_block_ptr(v_new + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, i_v * BV), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
    b_vn = tl.load(p_vn, boundary_check=(0, 1))
    b_o += tl.dot(b_A, b_vn)

    p_o = tl.make_block_ptr(o + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, i_v * BV), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_o, b_o.to(o.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))


def kda_forward(q, k, v, g, beta, scale, chunk_size=64):
    B, T, H, K = q.shape
    V = v.shape[-1]
    BT = chunk_size
    assert T % BT == 0
    NT = T // BT

    q = q.contiguous()
    k = k.contiguous()
    v = v.contiguous()
    g = g.contiguous()
    beta = beta.contiguous()

    dev = q.device
    qg = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)   # q * e^{gc} (for output)
    gclast = torch.empty(B, NT, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.float32)  # per-chunk total decay (for scan)
    w = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    u = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    kg = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    Aqk = torch.empty(B, T, H, BT, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    h = torch.empty(B, NT, H, K, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    v_new = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    o = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)

    # stage 1
    nstep = max(0, (BT - 1).bit_length() - 1)  # doubling steps to cover BT terms
    _intra_kernel[(NT, B * H)](
        q, k, v, g, beta, qg, gclast, w, u, kg, Aqk,
        T, NT, H, K, V, BT, nstep, scale,
        num_warps=8, num_stages=1,
    )

    # stage 2 (scan) -- small BV maximizes program count for the sequential scan.
    # Deeper software pipeline (ns=3) helps when occupancy is low (few programs)
    # or the chunk loop is long; otherwise ns=2 keeps it lean.
    BV = 16
    BK = 64
    scan_ns = 3 if (B * H <= 4 or NT >= 64) else 2
    _scan_kernel[(triton.cdiv(V, BV), B * H)](
        w, u, kg, gclast, h, v_new,
        T, NT, H, K, V, BT, BV, BK,
        num_warps=4, num_stages=scan_ns,
    )

    # stage 3 (output)
    BVo = 64
    BKo = 64
    _o_kernel[(triton.cdiv(V, BVo), NT, B * H)](
        qg, h, Aqk, v_new, o,
        T, NT, H, K, V, BT, BVo, BKo, scale,
        num_warps=4, num_stages=2,
    )

    return o


class Model(nn.Module):
    """KDA forward (chunk form). No learned parameters; all inputs are activations."""

    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
        super().__init__()
        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
        self.scale = float(K) ** -0.5
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1), persistent=False)

    def forward(self, q, k, v, g, beta):
        return kda_forward(q, k, v, g, beta, scale=self.scale, chunk_size=self.chunk_size)


# Module-level shape shims (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py per shape).
B = 2
T = 1024
H = 8
K = 128
V = 128
CHUNK_SIZE = 64


def get_inputs():
    torch.manual_seed(0)
    q = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    k = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    v = torch.randn(B, T, H, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    g = (torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.float32) * 0.1 - 0.05)
    beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B, T, H, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
    return [q, k, v, g, beta]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [B, T, H, K, V, CHUNK_SIZE]
Done. The final deliverable in `solution.py` passes `check.py` (PASS) and scores **peak_fraction 0.144, RESULT OK** on `benchmark.py`. ## What I built A hand-written 3-kernel Triton implementation of chunk-parallel Kimi Delta Attention (no FLA import — independent reimplementation), matching the reference math exactly. I first validated the decomposition with a pure-PyTorch "twin" (max_abs 3e-5 vs the naive reference) before touching Triton: 1. **intra** (parallel over b,h,chunk): within-chunk cumsum, the decayed score matrices `Aqk`/`Akk`, the `(I+Akk)⁻¹` inverse, and `w`, `u`, `kg`. 2. **scan** (parallel over b,h,V-block; sequential over chunks): the only serial part — produces per-chunk states `h` and `v_new = u − w@S`. 3. **output** (massively parallel): `o = scale·(q·e^{gc})@h + tril(Aqk)@v_new`. ## The result: 0.0064 → 0.144 (22x) The decisive fixes, in order of impact: - **Neumann-doubling inverse.** A naive 64-step forward-substitution triangular solve was catastrophic (8627us, 97% of runtime). Since `N=−Akk` is strictly lower-triangular it's nilpotent (`N⁶⁴=0`), so `(I+Akk)⁻¹ = ΣNⁱ = ∏(I+N^{2ʲ})` — 5 doubling steps of tensor-core matmuls instead of 64 serial scalar steps. Intra dropped 8627→183us. - **bf16 tensor-core operands + `num_warps=8`** for intra (fp32 dots overflowed the 99KB shared-memory limit; bf16 halves smem and 2x throughput, and nw=8 relieved register pressure). The generous 0.05 tolerance makes bf16 numerically free here. - **scan `BV=16` with occupancy-based `num_stages`.** The sequential scan is the only low-parallelism kernel; small V-blocks maximize program count, and a deeper pipeline when programs are few (thin batch) or the chunk loop is long. - **Store `q·e^{gc}` and a tiny `gc_last` instead of the full fp32 `gc`**, so the output kernel reads the pre-decayed query directly and skips re-reading `q`+`gc` and the exp. I confirmed fusing scan+output is a trap (0.057): it serializes the output's huge parallelism into the scan. Per-shape finals: short-context 0.147, headline T=2048 0.171, long T=4096 0.167, thin-batch 0.103 (the scan-bound anchor).

1	I need you to implement Kimi Delta Attention forward (chunk form) for the RTX 3090 (SM86 Ampere, GDDR6X, 936 GB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
2	
3	The op is the chunk-parallel KDA forward from the FLA library: q and k of shape (B, T, H, K) in bf16, v of shape (B, T, H, V) in bf16, g of shape (B, T, H, K) in fp32 (per-channel log-decay with in-chunk cumsum already applied), beta of shape (B, T, H) in bf16, scale a python float, chunk_size 64, no initial state, no final state. You return o of shape (B, T, H, V) in bf16. Correctness tolerance is 0.05 abs/rel — the long recurrence accumulates more error than a single GEMM so the bar's a bit looser than default bf16. The shapes you have to handle are B=2 T=1024 H=8 K=128 V=128 (short-context training step), B=2 T=2048 H=8 K=128 V=128 (the headline shape from the Kimi Linear paper), B=1 T=4096 H=8 K=128 V=128 (long context that stresses the inter-chunk recurrence), and B=1 T=2048 H=4 K=128 V=128 (thin batch decode).
4	
5	This needs to be a real custom kernel — the whole point of the problem is to write the chunk-parallel attention yourself, not call FLA's existing implementation. Don't import or call fla.ops.kda, fla.ops.

1	"""Naive PyTorch reference for Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form.
2	
3	This is the correctness oracle, NOT the SOTA baseline. It mirrors the
4	chunk-parallel formulation in fla/ops/kda/naive.py (Songlin Yang et al.)
5	without any Triton or CUDA optimization.
6	
7	Inputs (per the FLA convention):
8	  q, k : (B, T, H, K)   bf16   -- queries / keys
9	  v    : (B, T, H, V)   bf16   -- values
10	  g    : (B, T, H, K)   fp32   -- per-channel log-decay (in-chunk cumsum applied)
11	  beta : (B, T, H)      bf16   -- write strength
12	
13	Output:
14	  o    : (B, T, H, V)   bf16
15	
16	The agent must reproduce this output (within bf16 tolerance) using a CUTLASS
17	CuTe kernel on SM120 -- NOT by calling fla.ops.chunk_kda directly.
18	"""
19	from __future__ import annotations
20	
21	import torch
22	import torch.nn as nn
23	from einops import rearrange
24	
25	OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
26	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
27	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
28	
29	
30	def _naive_chunk_kda(
31	    q: torch.Tensor,
32	    k: torch.Tensor,
33	    v: torch.Tensor,
34	    g: torch.Tensor,
35	    beta: torch.Tensor,
36	    scale: float,
37	    chunk_size: int = 64,
38	) -> torch.Tensor:
39	    """KDA forward, no initial state, no final state. Returns o with v's dtype."""
40	    dtype = v.dtype
41	    B, T, H, K = q.shape
42	    V = v.shape[-1]
43	    BT = chunk_size
44	    assert T % BT == 0, f"T={T} must be a multiple of chunk_size={BT}"
45	    NT = T // BT

1	name: 02_kda_cutlass
2	display_name: "Kimi Delta Attention (chunk forward) via CUTLASS CuTe"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: compute
5	
6	# Approximate FLOPs per forward call. KDA forward (chunk form) breakdown per
7	# token across all heads:
8	#   - intra-chunk Aqk (q @ k.T with decay): 2*BT*K
9	#   - intra-chunk Akk + cumulative invert : ~3*BT*K + BT^2
10	#   - w = A @ (g.exp()*k):                  2*BT*K
11	#   - u = A @ v:                            2*BT*V
12	#   - inter-chunk q @ S:                    2*K*V
13	#   - inter-chunk (Aqk @ v_i):              2*BT*V
14	#   - state update S += k.T @ v_i:          2*K*V
15	# Aggregating with a constant of 4 (typical for chunked linear attention) gives
16	# the formula below. Used only for roofline reporting -- not graded directly.
17	flops_formula: "4 * B * T * H * (K*V + CHUNK_SIZE*K + CHUNK_SIZE*V)"
18	
19	# Bytes moved (lower bound): one read of q,k,v,g,beta and one write of o.
20	bytes_formula: "B*T*H*K*2 + B*T*H*K*2 + B*T*H*V*2 + B*T*H*K*4 + B*T*H*2 + B*T*H*V*2"
21	
22	hardware: [RTX_3090]
23	peak_tflops_key: bf16  # KDA's heavy work is bf16 @ bf16 -> fp32 GEMM-equivalent
24	peak_bandwidth_key: dram
25	
26	# bf16 default tolerance from src/eval/correctness.py is 1e-2 atol/rtol; KDA's
27	# long recurrence accumulates more error than a single GEMM, so we relax slightly.
28	tolerance:
29	  torch.bfloat16: 0.05  # was "5e-2" -- PyYAML parses un-dotted sci-notation as string
30	
31	# Forbidden ops -- using any in solution.py fails

1	"""NVIDIA GeForce RTX 3090 — GA102, SM86 (consumer Ampere), GDDR6X.
2	
3	Peak tensor-core throughputs are dense advertised peaks (NVIDIA Ampere GA102
4	whitepaper; sparse = 2x dense, not listed here). Real well-tuned kernels see
5	~60-85% of peak.
6	
7	Notes for grading on this part:
8	  - No FP8 and no FP4 tensor cores on Ampere (those debut on Ada sm_89 /
9	    Hopper sm_90). Those keys are intentionally absent: a problem that looks
10	    them up will KeyError, which correctly flags it as un-gradable here
11	    (01_fp8_gemm). bf16/fp16/int8/int4 tensor cores DO exist.
12	  - bf16/fp16 are the FP32-accumulate rate (71 TFLOPS dense). Consumer Ampere
13	    halves the FP32-accumulate tensor path vs the FP16-accumulate path (142
14	    dense); kernels held to the bf16 atol=0.02 tolerance need FP32 accumulate,
15	    so 71 is the realistic peak to grade against. cuBLAS bf16 GEMM lands at
16	    ~60 TFLOPS (~85% of 71), so peak_fraction stays <= 1.0.
17	  - The four memory-bound problems (03/05/07/09) grade on bandwidth, not these
18	    TFLOPS, so 936 GB/s is the number that matters for them.
19	"""

22	def _coerce_float(x):
23	    """Accept int/float/str scientific-notation as float; pass through dicts."""
24	    if isinstance(x, (int, float)):
25	        return float(x)
26	    if isinstance(x, str):
27	        try:
28	            return float(x)
29	        except ValueError:
30	            return x
31	    return x

41	    """
42	    # Accept several spellings of the same dty

1	"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.
2	
3	All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
4	implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.
5	
6	Methodology:
7	  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
8	    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
9	  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
10	    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
11	    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
12	  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
13	    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
14	  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.
15	
16	Notes / known biases not addressed here:
17	  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
18	    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
19	    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
20	    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
21	    "compiled" baseline policy.
22	  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
23	  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
24	    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
25	    instrumentation if you ever care.
26	"""
27	from __future__ import annotations
28	
29	import os
30	import re
31	

... (3182 more chars)

1	"""Roofline math: achieved TFLOPS / GB/s, peak fraction.
2	
3	FLOPS and bytes formulas come from the problem's `problem.yaml`. They are the
4	dense-equivalent algorithmic work; kernels that skip work (sparsity, early
5	exit) are still measured against the dense cost.
6	"""
7	from __future__ import annotations
8	
9	
10	def compute_tflops(flops: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
11	    """flops per invocation and wall time in ms -> TFLOPS."""
12	    if time_ms <= 0:
13	        return 0.0
14	    return flops / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e12
15	
16	
17	def compute_gbps(bytes_moved: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
18	    """bytes per invocation and wall time in ms -> GB/s."""
19	    if time_ms <= 0:
20	        return 0.0
21	    return bytes_moved / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e9
22	
23	
24	def peak_fraction(
25	    achieved: float,
26	    peak: float,
27	) -> float:
28	    """Return achieved / peak, clamped to [0, infinity)."""
29	    if peak <= 0:
30	        return 0.0
31	    return max(0.0, achieved / peak)
32

Critical detail: FLA uses `exp2` with the cumsum pre-scaled by `RCP_LN2` (1/ln2) purely to use the fast hardware exp2 - mathematically identical to `exp`. The decomposition is: cumsum g → intra (build A=(I-T)^{-1}, Aqk, w, u, kg, qg) → sequential state scan (h, v_new=u-w@S) → output (o = q_decay@h + Aqk@v_new). +++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_213324_claude_claude-opus-4-8_02_kda_cutlass/repo/problems/02_kda_cutlass/scratch_staged_ref.py

+"""Staged torch twin of the KDA chunk forward, structured exactly like my
+planned Triton kernels (exp2 + RCP_LN2, beta folded into rhs, exp split for
+decayed dot products, blocked layout). Validates against reference._naive_chunk_kda.
+
+Run: uv run python scratch_staged_ref.py
+"""
+import math
+
+import torch
+from einops import rearrange
+
+import reference
+
+RCP_LN2 = 1.0 / math.log(2.0)
+
+
+def staged_kda(q, k, v, g, beta, scale, BT=64):
+    """Mirror the 4-stage decomposition I will implement in Triton.
+
+    Inputs in (B,T,H,*) like the model. All compute in fp32. exp2-based.
+    """
+    B, T, H, K = q.shape
+    V = v.shape[-1]
+    NT = T // BT
+    dev = q.device
+
+    qf = q.float()
+    kf = k.float()
+    vf = v.float()
+    gf = g.float()
+    bf = beta.float()
+
+    # ---- Stage 0: in-chunk cumsum, scaled by RCP_LN2 so exp2(gc)=exp(cumsum) ----
+    # reshape to chunks
+    qc = rearrange(qf, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    kc = rearrange(kf, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    vc = rearrange(vf, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    gc = rearrange(gf, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    bc = rearrange(bf, "b (n c) h -> b h n c", c=BT)
+    gc = gc.cumsum(-2) * RCP_LN2  # (B,H,NT,BT,K)  exp2(gc) == exp(cumsum)
+
+    exp2 = lambda x: torch.exp2(x)
+
+    # ---- Stage 1: intra ----
+    # decayed factors (exp split)
+    eg = exp2(gc)          # exp(cumsum)            (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+    egn = exp2(-gc)        # exp(-cumsum)
+    qg = qc * eg           # q * exp(g)
+    kg_plus = kc * eg      # k * exp(g)
+    kg_minus = kc * egn    # k * exp(-g)
+
+    # Aqk[c,j] = scale * sum_d q[c,d] k[j,d] exp(gc[c,d]-gc[j,d]); mask j<=c
+    Aqk = torch.einsum("bhncd,bhnjd->bhncj", qg, kg_minus) * scale
+    idx = torch.arange(BT, device=dev)
+    mask_le = idx[:, None] >= idx[None, :]    # c>=j  (lower incl diag)
+    mask_lt = idx[:, None] > idx[None, :]     # c>j   (strict lower)
+    Aqk = torch.where(mask_le, Aqk, torch.zeros_like(Aqk))
+
+    # Akk[c,i] = beta[c] * sum_d k[c,d]k[i,d] exp(gc[c,d]-gc[i,d]); strict lower i<c
+    Akk = torch.einsum("bhncd,bhnid->bhnci", kg_plus, kg_minus) * bc[..., :, None]
+    Akk = torch.where(mask_lt, Akk, torch.zeros_like(Akk))
+
+    # invert (I + Akk): forward substitution (reference style)
+    A = -Akk
+    for i in range(1, BT):
+        A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i] + (A[..., i, :, None] * A[..., :, :i]).sum(-2)
+    eye = torch.eye(BT, device=dev)
+    Ainv = A + eye  # unit lower triangular  (B,H,NT,BT,BT)
+
+    # rhs (beta folded in)
+    rhs_w = bc[..., :, None] * kg_plus    # beta * k * exp(g)   (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+    rhs_u = bc[..., :, None] * vc         # beta * v            (B,H,NT,BT,V)
+    w = Ainv @ rhs_w                      # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+    u = Ainv @ rhs_u                      # (B,H,NT,BT,V)
+
+    # kg for state update: k * exp(gc_last - gc)
+    gc_last = gc[..., -1:, :]             # (B,H,NT,1,K)
+    kg = kc * exp2(gc_last - gc)          # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+
+    # ---- Stage 2: sequential scan ----
+    S = torch.zeros(B, H, K, V, device=dev)
+    h = torch.zeros(B, H, NT, K, V, device=dev)
+    v_new = torch.zeros(B, H, NT, BT, V, device=dev)
+    for i in range(NT):
+        h[:, :, i] = S
+        vn = u[:, :, i] - w[:, :, i] @ S            # (B,H,BT,V)
+        v_new[:, :, i] = vn
+        decay = exp2(gc_last[:, :, i, 0])           # (B,H,K)
+        S = S * decay[..., :, None]
+        S = S + kg[:, :, i].transpose(-1, -2) @ vn  # (B,H,K,V)
+
+    # ---- Stage 3: output ----
+    o = torch.zeros(B, H, NT, BT, V, device=dev)
+    for i in range(NT):
+        o_inter = (qg[:, :, i] @ h[:, :, i]) * scale
+        o_intra = Aqk[:, :, i] @ v_new[:, :, i]
+        o[:, :, i] = o_inter + o_intra
+
+    o = rearrange(o, "b h n c d -> b (n c) h d")
+    return o
+
+
+def main():
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    dev = "cuda"
+    for (B, T, H, K, V) in [(2, 1024, 8, 128, 128), (1, 256, 4, 128, 128)]:
+        reference.B, reference.T, reference.H, reference.K, reference.V = B, T, H, K, V
+        q, k, v, g, beta = [x.to(dev) for x in reference.get_inputs()]
+        scale = float(K) ** -0.5
+        ref = reference._naive_chunk_kda(q, k, v, g, beta, scale=scale, chunk_size=64)
+        out = staged_kda(q, k, v, g, beta, scale).to(ref.dtype)
+        diff = (ref.float() - out.float()).abs()
+        rel = diff / ref.float().abs().clamp_min(1e-6)
+        print(f"shape B{B} T{T} H{H}: max_abs={diff.max().item():.3e} "
+              f"max_rel={rel.max().item():.3e} mean_abs={diff.mean().item():.3e}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

+"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form, custom Triton kernels.
+
+Hand-written chunk-parallel KDA for RTX 3090 (SM86). Implements the same
+decomposition the FLA library uses, but as my own Triton kernels (no fla import):
+
+  stage 1 (intra, parallel over b,h,chunk):
+      gc = cumsum(g) within chunk;
+      Aqk[c,j] = scale*<q_c e^{gc_c-gc_j}, k_j>   (j<=c)
+      Akk[c,i] = beta_c*<k_c e^{gc_c-gc_i}, k_i>  (i<c, strict lower)
+      Ainv = (I + Akk)^{-1}    (forward substitution, fp32)
+      w = Ainv @ (beta * k * e^{gc});  u = Ainv @ (beta * v)
+      kg = k * e^{gc_last - gc}
+  stage 2 (scan, parallel over b,h,v-block; sequential over chunks):
+      h[i] = S;  v_new = u - w@S;  S = diag(e^{gc_last})S + kg^T @ v_new
+  stage 3 (output, parallel over b,h,chunk,v-block):
+      o = scale*(q e^{gc}) @ h + tril(Aqk) @ v_new
+
+Reference: fla.ops.kda (Songlin Yang et al.); this is an independent reimpl.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# stage 1: intra-chunk (cumsum, Aqk, Akk, inverse, w, u, kg)
+# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+@triton.jit
+def _intra_kernel(
+    q, k, v, g, beta,
+    gc, w, u, kg, Aqk,
+    T,
+    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
+    scale,
+):
+    i_t = tl.program_id(0)
+    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
+    i_b = i_bh // H
+    i_h = i_bh % H
+
+    qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
+    v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
+    b_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h)
+    a_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * BT
+
+    o_t = tl.arange(0, BT)
+
+    # ---- cumsum g within chunk ----
+    p_g = tl.make_block_ptr(g + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    b_g = tl.load(p_g, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    b_gc = tl.cumsum(b_g, axis=0)  # (BT, K)
+    p_gc = tl.make_block_ptr(gc + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_gc, b_gc.to(gc.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+    # last-row cumsum (chunk total decay)
+    b_gc_last = tl.sum(tl.where((o_t == (BT - 1))[:, None], b_gc, 0.0), 0)  # (K,)
+
+    eg = tl.exp(b_gc)         # e^{gc}
+    egn = tl.exp(-b_gc)       # e^{-gc}
+
+    p_q = tl.make_block_ptr(q + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_k = tl.make_block_ptr(k + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_v = tl.make_block_ptr(v + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
+    b_q = tl.load(p_q, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    b_k = tl.load(p_k, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    b_v = tl.load(p_v, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+
+    p_beta = tl.make_block_ptr(beta + b_base, (T,), (H,), (i_t * BT,), (BT,), (0,))
+    b_beta = tl.load(p_beta, boundary_check=(0,)).to(tl.float32)
+
+    b_qg = b_q * eg
+    b_kgp = b_k * eg
+    b_kgm = b_k * egn
+
+    # Aqk (BT,BT), lower incl diag, scaled
+    b_Aqk = tl.dot(b_qg, tl.trans(b_kgm), input_precision="ieee") * scale
+    m_le = o_t[:, None] >= o_t[None, :]
+    b_Aqk = tl.where(m_le, b_Aqk, 0.0)
+    p_Aqk = tl.make_block_ptr(Aqk + a_base, (T, BT), (H * BT, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_Aqk, b_Aqk.to(Aqk.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+    # Akk strict lower (L), fp32
+    b_Akk = tl.dot(b_kgp, tl.trans(b_kgm), input_precision="ieee") * b_beta[:, None]
+    m_lt = o_t[:, None] > o_t[None, :]
+    b_L = tl.where(m_lt, b_Akk, 0.0)
+
+    # ---- forward-substitution inverse of (I + L) ----
+    b_Ai = -b_L
+    for i in range(2, BT):
+        b_row = -tl.sum(tl.where((o_t == i)[:, None], b_L, 0.0), 0)  # -L[i,:]
+        b_row = tl.where(o_t < i, b_row, 0.0)
+        b_row += tl.sum(b_row[:, None] * b_Ai, 0)
+        b_Ai = tl.where((o_t == i)[:, None], b_row, b_Ai)
+    b_Ai += (o_t[:, None] == o_t[None, :]).to(tl.float32)
+
+    # ---- w, u ----
+    b_rhs_w = (b_beta[:, None] * b_kgp).to(w.dtype.element_ty)
+    b_rhs_u = (b_beta[:, None] * b_v).to(u.dtype.element_ty)
+    b_Ai_c = b_Ai.to(w.dtype.element_ty)
+    b_w = tl.dot(b_Ai_c, b_rhs_w)
+    b_u = tl.dot(b_Ai_c, b_rhs_u)
+    p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(w + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(u + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_w, b_w.to(w.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+    tl.store(p_u, b_u.to(u.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+    # ---- kg = k * e^{gc_last - gc} ----
+    b_kg = b_k * tl.exp(b_gc_last[None, :] - b_gc)
+    p_kg = tl.make_block_ptr(kg + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_kg, b_kg.to(kg.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+
+# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# stage 2: sequential state scan -> h (per chunk state), v_new
+# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+@triton.jit
+def _scan_kernel(
+    w, u, kg, gc, h, v_new,
+    T, NT,
+    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
+    BV: tl.constexpr, BK: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    i_v = tl.program_id(0)
+    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
+    i_b = i_bh // H
+    i_h = i_bh % H
+
+    o_k = tl.arange(0, K)
+
+    # state accumulator (K, BV) fp32, K split into BK-blocks handled as full K here
+    b_h = tl.zeros([K, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for i_t in range(NT):
+        qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
+        v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
+        h_base = ((i_b * NT + i_t) * H + i_h) * K * V
+
+        # store current state to h[i_t]
+        p_h = tl.make_bl

... (5954 more chars)

+"""Quick correctness check: my Triton kda_forward vs reference naive."""
+import torch
+
+import reference
+import solution
+
+
+def run(B, T, H, K, V, scales=(1.0,)):
+    reference.B, reference.T, reference.H, reference.K, reference.V = B, T, H, K, V
+    dev = "cuda"
+    q, k, v, g, beta = [x.to(dev) for x in reference.get_inputs()]
+    scale = float(K) ** -0.5
+    for s in scales:
+        qs, ks, vs = q * s, k * s, v * s
+        ref = reference._naive_chunk_kda(qs, ks, vs, g, beta, scale=scale, chunk_size=64)
+        out = solution.kda_forward(qs, ks, vs, g, beta, scale=scale, chunk_size=64)
+        out = out.to(ref.dtype)
+        diff = (ref.float() - out.float()).abs()
+        denom = ref.float().abs().clamp_min(1e-6)
+        rel = (diff / denom)
+        ok = torch.allclose(ref.float(), out.float(), atol=5e-2, rtol=5e-2)
+        print(f"B{B} T{T} H{H} scale{s}: max_abs={diff.max().item():.3e} "
+              f"mean_abs={diff.mean().item():.3e} max_rel={rel.max().item():.3e} "
+              f"allclose(0.05)={ok}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    run(1, 256, 4, 128, 128)
+    run(2, 128, 8, 128, 128)
+    run(2, 1024, 8, 128, 128)
+    run(1, 2048, 4, 128, 128, scales=(1.0, 0.01, 2.0))

-Reference: fla.ops.kda (Songlin Yang et al.); this is an independent reimpl.
 """
 from __future__ import annotations

+"""KDA forward, chunk form, custom Triton kernels (v2: fused scan+output).
+
+Two kernels:
+  stage 1 (intra, parallel b,h,chunk): Aqk, Ainv, w, u, kg  (gc not materialized)
+  stage 2 (scan+output fused, parallel b,h,v-block; sequential chunks):
+      per chunk: v_new=u-w@S; o = scale*(q e^{gc})@S + tril(Aqk)@v_new;
+                 S = diag(e^{gc_last})S + kg^T@v_new
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _intra_kernel(
+    q, k, v, g, beta,
+    w, u, kg, Aqk,
+    T,
+    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
+    scale,
+):
+    i_t = tl.program_id(0)
+    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
+    i_b = i_bh // H
+    i_h = i_bh % H
+
+    qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
+    v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
+    b_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h)
+    a_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * BT
+
+    o_t = tl.arange(0, BT)
+
+    p_g = tl.make_block_ptr(g + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    b_g = tl.load(p_g, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    b_gc = tl.cumsum(b_g, axis=0)
+    b_gc_last = tl.sum(tl.where((o_t == (BT - 1))[:, None], b_gc, 0.0), 0)
+
+    eg = tl.exp(b_gc)
+    egn = tl.exp(-b_gc)
+
+    p_q = tl.make_block_ptr(q + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_k = tl.make_block_ptr(k + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_v = tl.make_block_ptr(v + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
+    b_q = tl.load(p_q, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    b_k = tl.load(p_k, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    b_v = tl.load(p_v, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+
+    p_beta = tl.make_block_ptr(beta + b_base, (T,), (H,), (i_t * BT,), (BT,), (0,))
+    b_beta = tl.load(p_beta, boundary_check=(0,)).to(tl.float32)
+
+    b_qg = b_q * eg
+    b_kgp = b_k * eg
+    b_kgm = b_k * egn
+
+    b_Aqk = tl.dot(b_qg, tl.trans(b_kgm), input_precision="ieee") * scale
+    m_le = o_t[:, None] >= o_t[None, :]
+    b_Aqk = tl.where(m_le, b_Aqk, 0.0)
+    p_Aqk = tl.make_block_ptr(Aqk + a_base, (T, BT), (H * BT, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_Aqk, b_Aqk.to(Aqk.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+    b_Akk = tl.dot(b_kgp, tl.trans(b_kgm), input_precision="ieee") * b_beta[:, None]
+    m_lt = o_t[:, None] > o_t[None, :]
+    b_L = tl.where(m_lt, b_Akk, 0.0)
+
+    b_Ai = -b_L
+    for i in range(2, BT):
+        b_row = -tl.sum(tl.where((o_t == i)[:, None], b_L, 0.0), 0)
+        b_row = tl.where(o_t < i, b_row, 0.0)
+        b_row += tl.sum(b_row[:, None] * b_Ai, 0)
+        b_Ai = tl.where((o_t == i)[:, None], b_row, b_Ai)
+    b_Ai += (o_t[:, None] == o_t[None, :]).to(tl.float32)
+
+    b_rhs_w = (b_beta[:, None] * b_kgp).to(w.dtype.element_ty)
+    b_rhs_u = (b_beta[:, None] * b_v).to(u.dtype.element_ty)
+    b_Ai_c = b_Ai.to(w.dtype.element_ty)
+    b_w = tl.dot(b_Ai_c, b_rhs_w)
+    b_u = tl.dot(b_Ai_c, b_rhs_u)
+    p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(w + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(u + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_w, b_w.to(w.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+    tl.store(p_u, b_u.to(u.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+    b_kg = b_k * tl.exp(b_gc_last[None, :] - b_gc)
+    p_kg = tl.make_block_ptr(kg + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_kg, b_kg.to(kg.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _scan_o_kernel(
+    q, g, w, u, kg, Aqk, o,
+    T, NT,
+    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr, BT: tl.constexpr,
+    BV: tl.constexpr,
+    scale,
+):
+    i_v = tl.program_id(0)
+    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
+    i_b = i_bh // H
+    i_h = i_bh % H
+
+    o_t = tl.arange(0, BT)
+    m_le = o_t[:, None] >= o_t[None, :]
+
+    b_S = tl.zeros([K, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for i_t in range(NT):
+        qk_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * K
+        v_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * V
+        a_base = (i_b * T * H + i_h) * BT
+
+        # recompute gc
+        p_g = tl.make_block_ptr(g + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+        b_g = tl.load(p_g, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+        b_gc = tl.cumsum(b_g, axis=0)
+        b_gc_last = tl.sum(tl.where((o_t == (BT - 1))[:, None], b_gc, 0.0), 0)
+
+        # v_new = u - w@S
+        p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(w + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+        b_w = tl.load(p_w, boundary_check=(0, 1))
+        b_wh = tl.dot(b_w, b_S.to(b_w.dtype))
+        p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(u + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, i_v * BV), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
+        b_vn = tl.load(p_u, boundary_check=(0, 1)) - b_wh
+        b_vn_b = b_vn.to(q.dtype.element_ty)
+
+        # output
+        p_q = tl.make_block_ptr(q + qk_base, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+        b_q = tl.load(p_q, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+        b_qg = (b_q * tl.exp(b_gc)).to(q.dtype.element_ty)
+        b_o = tl.dot(b_qg, b_S.to(q.dtype.element_ty)) * scale
+        p_A = tl.make_block_ptr(Aqk + a_base, (T, BT), (H * BT, 1), (i_t * BT, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
+        b_A = tl.load(p_A, boundary_check=(0, 1))
+        b_A = tl.where(m_le, b_A, 0.0).to(q.dtype.element_ty)
+        b_o += tl.dot(b_A, b_vn_b)
+        p_o = tl.make_block_ptr(o + v_base, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (i_t * BT, i_v * BV), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
+        tl.store(p_o, b_o.to(o.dtype.element_ty), boundary_check=(0, 1))
+
+        # state update
+        b_S = b_S * tl.exp(b_gc_last)[:, None]
+        p_kg = tl.make_block_ptr(kg + qk_base, (K, T), (1, H * K), (0, i_t * BT),

... (2144 more chars)

+"""Per-kernel timing to find the bottleneck."""
+import torch
+import triton
+
+import reference
+import solution as S
+
+
+def time_call(fn, iters=50, warmup=20):
+    for _ in range(warmup):
+        fn()
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    e0 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
+    e1 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
+    e0.record()
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        fn()
+    e1.record()
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    return e0.elapsed_time(e1) / iters
+
+
+def main():
+    B, T, H, K, V = 2, 2048, 8, 128, 128
+    BT = 64
+    NT = T // BT
+    reference.B, reference.T, reference.H, reference.K, reference.V = B, T, H, K, V
+    dev = "cuda"
+    q, k, v, g, beta = [x.to(dev).contiguous() for x in reference.get_inputs()]
+    scale = float(K) ** -0.5
+
+    gc = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.float32)
+    w = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    u = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    kg = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    Aqk = torch.empty(B, T, H, BT, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    h = torch.empty(B, NT, H, K, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    v_new = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    o = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+
+    def intra():
+        S._intra_kernel[(NT, B * H)](q, k, v, g, beta, gc, w, u, kg, Aqk, T, H, K, V, BT, scale,
+                                     num_warps=4, num_stages=2)
+
+    def scan():
+        S._scan_kernel[(triton.cdiv(V, 64), B * H)](w, u, kg, gc, h, v_new, T, NT, H, K, V, BT, 64, 64,
+                                                    num_warps=4, num_stages=2)
+
+    def out():
+        S._o_kernel[(triton.cdiv(V, 64), NT, B * H)](q, gc, h, Aqk, v_new, o, T, NT, H, K, V, BT, 64, 64, scale,

Confirmed: **intra = 8627us (97% of runtime)**; scan + out are already fast (200us combined). The 62-iteration serial inverse with per-iter (64,64) reductions is O(BT³) of slow scalar work. I'll replace it with a **log-depth doubling inverse**: since `N=-L` is strictly-lower (nilpotent, N⁶⁴=0), `(I+L)⁻¹ = Σ Nⁱ = ∏(I+N^{2ʲ})`, computed in 5 doubling steps of tensor-core matmuls instead of 62 serial steps.

@@ -0,0 +1,32 @@
+---
+name: kbhard-kda-cutlass-triton-approach
+description: How to implement 02_kda_cutlass (Kimi Delta Attention) fast on the 3090 - Triton 3-stage chunk-parallel + Neumann-doubling inverse
+metadata:
+  type: project
+---
+
+02_kda_cutlass = chunk-parallel Kimi Delta Attention forward (gated delta rule,
+per-channel decay). Reference math == fla.ops.kda.naive.naive_chunk_kda (read
+it; the prose in PROMPT.txt about "cumsum already applied" is misleading - the
+Model does `g.cumsum` itself).
+
+Winning structure (my own Triton, NOT importing fla; forbidden grep blocks
+"fla.ops.kda"/"chunk_kda"/etc even in COMMENTS):
+- stage 1 intra (parallel b,h,chunk): cumsum g; Aqk[c,j]=scale<q_c e^{gc_c-gc_j},k_j> (j<=c);
+  Akk strict-lower; Ainv=(I+Akk)^{-1}; w=Ainv@(beta k e^{gc}); u=Ainv@(beta v); kg=k e^{gc_last-gc}.
+- stage 2 scan (parallel b,h,v-block; SEQUENTIAL chunks): h[i]=S; v_new=u-w@S;
+  S=diag(e^{gc_last})S + kg^T@v_new.
+- stage 3 out (parallel b,h,chunk,v-block): o=scale(q e^{gc})@h + tril(Aqk)@v_new.
+- Stage2+3 fuse cleanly per v-block (saves h/v_new global round-trip).
+
+CRITICAL perf gotcha: the (I+Akk) inverse. A naive 64-step forward-substitution
+loop in Triton = 8.6ms (97% of runtime), catastrophic. Fix: N=-Akk is strictly
+lower => nilpotent (N^64=0), so (I+Akk)^{-1}=sum N^i=prod_j(I+N^{2^j}). Do
+log2(64)-1=5 doubling steps, each two 64x64 tensor-core matmuls. tf32 dots are
+fine for the 0.05 tol.
+
+Grading: regime=compute, peak bf16=71 TFLOPS (3090). flops=4*B*T*H*(K*V+CHUNK*K+CHUNK*V).
+Tol 0.05 nominal is GENEROUS; bf16 tensor cores + fp32 accumulate pass easily.
+stress small_qkv (x0.01, atol 5e-4) is trivially easy (outputs tiny vs atol);
+large_qkv (x2, atol/rtol 5e-2) fine since g/beta unscaled so exp factors bounded.
+See [[kbhard-kda-on-3090]] for the (older, RTX-PRO-6000-graded) ceiling note.

import torch, reference, solution
torch.manual_seed(0)
# fast correctness vs staged torch twin (avoids slow naive python loops at T=2048)
import scratch_staged_ref as sr
for (B,T,H) in [(1,512,4),(2,1024,8),(1,2048,8)]:
    reference.B,reference.T,reference.H,reference.K,reference.V=B,T,H,128,128
    q,k,v,g,beta=[x.cuda() for x in reference.get_inputs()]
    sc=128**-0.5
    for s in (1.0,0.01,2.0):
        ref=sr.staged_kda(q*s,k*s,v*s,g,beta,sc).to(torch.bfloat16)
        out=solution.kda_forward(q*s,k*s,v*s,g,beta,sc)
        d=(ref.float()-out.float()).abs()
        ok=torch.allclose(ref.float(),out.float(),atol=5e-2,rtol=5e-2)
        print(f'B{B}T{T}H{H} s{s}: max_abs={d.max().item():.2e} allclose={ok}')

+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_213324_claude_claude-opus-4-8_02_kda_cutlass/repo/problems/02_kda_cutlass/scratch_bench_mod.py
@@ -0,0 +1,63 @@
+"""Benchmark an arbitrary solution module across all 4 shapes (median ms + fraction).
+
+Usage: uv run python scratch_bench_mod.py <module_name>
+e.g.    uv run python scratch_bench_mod.py scratch_solution_v2
+"""
+import importlib
+import statistics
+import sys
+
+import torch
+
+import reference
+
+SHAPES = [
+    (2, 1024, 8, 128, 128),
+    (2, 2048, 8, 128, 128),
+    (1, 4096, 8, 128, 128),
+    (1, 2048, 4, 128, 128),
+]
+PEAK = 71.0e12
+
+
+def flops(B, T, H, K, V, C=64):
+    return 4 * B * T * H * (K * V + C * K + C * V)
+
+
+def time_fn(fn, inputs, iters=30, warmup=15):
+    for _ in range(warmup):
+        fn(*inputs)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    ts = []
+    flush = torch.empty(32 * 1024 * 1024, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        flush.zero_()
+        torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        e0 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
+        e1 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
+        e0.record()
+        fn(*inputs)
+        e1.record()
+        torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        ts.append(e0.elapsed_time(e1))
+    return statistics.median(ts)
+
+
+def main():
+    mod = importlib.import_module(sys.argv[1])
+    fracs = []
+    for (B, T, H, K, V) in SHAPES:
+        reference.B, reference.T, reference.H, reference.K, reference.V = B, T, H, K, V
+        q, k, v, g, beta = [x.cuda() for x in reference.get_inputs()]
+        sc = K ** -0.5
+        ms = time_fn(lambda *a: mod.kda_forward(*a, sc), (q, k, v, g, beta))
+        tf = flops(B, T, H, K, V) / (ms * 1e-3) / 1e12
+        fr = tf / (PEAK / 1e12)
+        fracs.append(fr)
+        print(f"B{B}T{T}H{H}: ms={ms:.3f} tflops={tf:.2f} frac={fr:.4f}")
+    gm = statistics.geometric_mean(fracs)
+    print(f"GEOMEAN frac={gm:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_213324_claude_claude-opus-4-8_02_kda_cutlass/repo/problems/02_kda_cutlass/scratch_tune.py
@@ -0,0 +1,87 @@
+"""Tune full 3-kernel pipeline: per shape, sweep scan/out BV and num_warps.
+
+Reports total ms + peak_fraction so I can see the geomean impact directly.
+"""
+import statistics
+
+import torch
+import triton
+
+import reference
+import solution as S
+
+SHAPES = [
+    (2, 1024, 8, 128, 128),
+    (2, 2048, 8, 128, 128),
+    (1, 4096, 8, 128, 128),
+    (1, 2048, 4, 128, 128),
+]
+PEAK = 71.0e12
+
+
+def flops(B, T, H, K, V, C=64):
+    return 4 * B * T * H * (K * V + C * K + C * V)
+
+
+def time_fn(fn, iters=40, warmup=15):
+    for _ in range(warmup):
+        fn()
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    ts = []
+    flush = torch.empty(32 * 1024 * 1024, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        flush.zero_(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        e0 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True); e1 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
+        e0.record(); fn(); e1.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        ts.append(e0.elapsed_time(e1))
+    return statistics.median(ts)
+
+
+def make_pipeline(B, T, H, K, V, scan_bv, scan_nw, scan_ns, out_bv, out_nw, out_ns, intra_nw):
+    BT = 64
+    NT = T // BT
+    dev = "cuda"
+    reference.B, reference.T, reference.H, reference.K, reference.V = B, T, H, K, V
+    q, k, v, g, beta = [x.to(dev).contiguous() for x in reference.get_inputs()]
+    scale = K ** -0.5
+    nstep = max(0, (BT - 1).bit_length() - 1)
+    gc = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.float32)
+    w = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    u = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    kg = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    Aqk = torch.empty(B, T, H, BT, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    h = torch.empty(B, NT, H, K, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    v_new = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    o = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+
+    def run():
+        S._intra_kernel[(NT, B * H)](q, k, v, g, beta, gc, w, u, kg, Aqk, T, H, K, V, BT, nstep, scale,
+                                     num_warps=intra_nw, num_stages=1)
+        S._scan_kernel[(triton.cdiv(V, scan_bv), B * H)](w, u, kg, gc, h, v_new, T, NT, H, K, V, BT, scan_bv, 64,
+                                                         num_warps=scan_nw, num_stages=scan_ns)
+        S._o_kernel[(triton.cdiv(V, out_bv), NT, B * H)](q, gc, h, Aqk, v_new, o, T, NT, H, K, V, BT, out_bv, 64, scale,
+                                                        num_warps=out_nw, num_stages=out_ns)
+    return run
+
+
+def main():
+    configs = [
+        ("base   sbv64", dict(scan_bv=64, scan_nw=4, scan_ns=2, out_bv=64, out_nw=4, out_ns=2, intra_nw=8)),
+        ("scan32     ", dict(scan_bv=32, scan_nw=4, scan_ns=2, out_bv=64, out_nw=4, out_ns=2, intra_nw=8)),
+        ("scan32 nw2 ", dict(scan_bv=32, scan_nw=2, scan_ns=2, out_bv=64, out_nw=4, out_ns=2, intra_nw=8)),
+        ("out128     ", dict(scan_bv=64, scan_nw=4, scan_ns=2, out_bv=128, out_nw=4, out_ns=2, intra_nw=8)),
+        ("scan32 out128", dict(scan_bv=32, scan_nw=4, scan_ns=2, out_bv=128, out_nw=4, out_ns=2, intra_nw=8)),
+    ]
+    for name, cfg in configs:
+        fracs = []
+        for (B, T, H, K, V) in SHAPES:
+            run = make_pipeline(B, T, H, K, V, **cfg)
+            ms = time_fn(run)
+            fr = flops(B, T, H, K, V) / (ms * 1e-3) / PEAK
+            fracs.append(fr)
+        gm = statistics.geometric_mean(fracs)
+        print(f"{name}: " + " ".join(f"{f:.3f}" for f in fracs) + f"  GM={gm:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

+kernels. num_stages=1 for intra (fp32 tiles blow 99KB smem at ns=2); bf16 dot

--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_213324_claude_claude-opus-4-8_02_kda_cutlass/repo/problems/02_kda_cutlass/scratch_ablate.py

+"""Ablate intra (doubling on/off) and measure FLA ceiling if available."""
+import statistics
+import torch
+import triton
+import reference
+import solution as S
+
+
+def tc(fn, iters=60, warmup=25):
+    for _ in range(warmup):
+        fn()
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    e0 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True); e1 = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
+    e0.record()
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        fn()
+    e1.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    return e0.elapsed_time(e1) / iters
+
+
+def setup(B, T, H, K, V):
+    BT = 64; NT = T // BT; dev = "cuda"
+    reference.B, reference.T, reference.H, reference.K, reference.V = B, T, H, K, V
+    q, k, v, g, beta = [x.to(dev).contiguous() for x in reference.get_inputs()]
+    return q, k, v, g, beta, BT, NT
+
+
+def main():
+    B, T, H, K, V = 2, 2048, 8, 128, 128
+    q, k, v, g, beta, BT, NT = setup(B, T, H, K, V)
+    scale = K ** -0.5
+    dev = "cuda"
+    gc = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.float32)
+    w = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    u = torch.empty(B, T, H, V, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    kg = torch.empty(B, T, H, K, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    Aqk = torch.empty(B, T, H, BT, device=dev, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    for ns in (5, 0):
+        t = tc(lambda ns=ns: S._intra_kernel[(NT, B * H)](q, k, v, g, beta, gc, w, u, kg, Aqk, T, H, K, V, BT, ns, scale, num_warps=8, num_stages=1))
+        print(f"intra nstep={ns}: {t*1000:.0f}us")
+
+    # FLA ceiling
+    try:
+        from fla.ops.kda import chunk_kda
+        def fla():
+            chunk_kda(q=q, k=k, v=v, g=g, beta=beta, scale=scale, initial_state=None,
+                      output_final_state=False, use_qk_l2norm_in_kernel=False, use_gate_in_kernel=False)
+        # warmup includes cumsum mismatch? FLA expects pre-cumsum? It does chunk_local_cumsum internally.
+        t = tc(fla, iters=30, warmup=15)
+        flops = 4 * B * T * H * (K * V + 64 * K + 64 * V)
+        print(f"FLA chunk_kda s1: {t*1000:.0f}us  frac={flops/(t*1e-3)/71e12:.4f}")
+    except Exception as e:
+        print(f"FLA unavailable: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

stdout (22 chars)
Updated task #5 status
assistant
Done. The final deliverable in `solution.py` passes `check.py` (PASS) and scores **peak_fraction 0.144, RESULT OK** on `benchmark.py`. ## What I built A hand-written 3-kernel Triton implementation of chunk-parallel Kimi Delta Attention (no FLA import — independent reimplementation), matching the reference math exactly. I first validated the decomposition with a pure-PyTorch "twin" (max_abs 3e-5 vs the naive reference) before touching Triton: 1. **intra** (parallel over b,h,chunk): within-chunk cumsum, the decayed score matrices `Aqk`/`Akk`, the `(I+Akk)⁻¹` inverse, and `w`, `u`, `kg`. 2. **scan** (parallel over b,h,V-block; sequential over chunks): the only serial part — produces per-chunk states `h` and `v_new = u − w@S`. 3. **output** (massively parallel): `o = scale·(q·e^{gc})@h + tril(Aqk)@v_new`. ## The result: 0.0064 → 0.144 (22x) The decisive fixes, in order of impact: - **Neumann-doubling inverse.** A naive 64-step forward-substitution triangular solve was catastrophic (8627us, 97% of runtime). Since `N=−Akk` is strictly lower-triangular it's nilpotent (`N⁶⁴=0`), so `(I+Akk)⁻¹ = ΣNⁱ = ∏(I+N^{2ʲ})` — 5 doubling steps of tensor-core matmuls instead of 64 serial scalar steps. Intra dropped 8627→183us. - **bf16 tensor-core operands + `num_warps=8`** for intra (fp32 dots overflowed the 99KB shared-memory limit; bf16 halves smem and 2x throughput, and nw=8 relieved register pressure). The generous 0.05 tolerance makes bf16 numerically free here. - **scan `BV=16` with occupancy-based `num_stages`.** The sequential scan is the only low-parallelism kernel; small V-blocks maximize program count, and a deeper pipeline when programs are few (thin batch) or the chunk loop is long. - **Store `q·e^{gc}` and a tiny `gc_last` instead of the full fp32 `gc`**, so the output kernel reads the pre-decayed query directly and skips re-reading `q`+`gc` and the exp. I confirmed fusing scan+output is a trap (0.057): it serializes the output's huge parallelism into the scan. Per-shape finals: short-context 0.147, headline T=2048 0.171, long T=4096 0.167, thin-batch 0.103 (the scan-bound anchor).
in 2out 4cache_r 427237cache_w 717
